<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">List of sports rivalries</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Original_research" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="" data-file-height="40" data-file-width="40" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>possibly contains <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research">original research</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_sports_rivalries&amp;action=edit">improve it</a> by <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verifying</a> the claims made and adding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Inline_citations" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">inline citations</a>. Statements consisting only of original research should be removed.</span> <small><i>(April 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote plainlinks" role="note">This list is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Lists#Incomplete_lists" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Lists">incomplete</a>; you can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_sports_rivalries&amp;action=edit">expanding it</a>.</div>
<p>A <b>sports rivalry</b> is intense competition between athletic teams or athletes. This pressure of competition is felt by players, coaches, and management, but is perhaps felt strongest by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fan_(aficionado)" title="Fan (aficionado)">fans</a>. The intensity of the rivalry varies from a friendly competition on one end to serious violence on the other that, in one case (the <a href="/wiki/Football_War" title="Football War">Football War</a>), was suggested to have led to military conflicts. Owners typically encourage rivalries as they tend to improve game attendance and <a href="/wiki/Audience_measurement" title="Audience measurement">television ratings</a> for rivalry matches, but a rivalry that gets out of control can lead to <a href="/wiki/Violence_in_sports" title="Violence in sports">fighting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Football_hooliganism" title="Football hooliganism">hooliganism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riot" title="Riot">rioting</a> and some, with career-ending or even fatal consequences.</p>
<p>Rivalries stem from various sources. Simple geographic proximity as well as frequent meetings in important games can lead to rivalries. Games between two rivals of close geographical proximity are usually called a <b>local derby</b>, or simply just <b>derby</b> (<small>UK:</small> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɑːr/ 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/i/ 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <span title="English pronunciation respelling"><a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i><b><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">DAR</span></span></b>-bee</i></a></span> or <small>US:</small> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɜːr/ 'ur' in 'fur'">ɜːr</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/i/ 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <span title="English pronunciation respelling"><a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i><b><span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">DER</span></span></b>-bee</i></a></span>); a sporting fixture between two teams from the same town, city or region, particularly in <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a>. The phrase most likely originated from <a href="/wiki/Derby_(horse_race)" title="Derby (horse race)">The Derby</a>, a horse race in England, founded by the <a href="/wiki/Edward_Smith-Stanley,_12th_Earl_of_Derby" title="Edward Smith-Stanley, 12th Earl of Derby">12th Earl of Derby</a> in 1780, since at least as early as 1840 'derby' has been used as a noun in English to denote any kind of sporting contest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> It was renowned as the site of a chaotic and exuberant game that involved the whole town and often resulted in fatalities. The goals were at Nuns Mill in the north and the Gallows Balk in the south of the town, and much of the action took place in the <a href="/wiki/River_Derwent,_Derbyshire" title="River Derwent, Derbyshire">River Derwent</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Markeaton_Brook" title="Markeaton Brook">Markeaton Brook</a>. Nominally the players came from All Saints' and St Peter's parishes, but in practice the game was a <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/free-for-all" title="wiktionary:free-for-all">free-for-all</a> with as many as 1,000 players. A Frenchman who observed the match in 1829 wrote in horror, 'if Englishmen call this play, it would be impossible to say what they call fighting'. The traditional Shrovetide football match is commonplace in the town of <a href="/wiki/Ashbourne,_Derbyshire" title="Ashbourne, Derbyshire">Ashbourne, Derbyshire</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexican_Baseball_League">Mexican Baseball League</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_sports_rivalries&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Mexican Baseball League">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Diablos_Rojos_del_M%C3%A9xico" title="Diablos Rojos del México">Diablos Rojos del México (Mexico City Red Devils)</a> vs. <a href="/wiki/Tigres_de_Quintana_Roo" title="Tigres de Quintana Roo">Tigres de Quintana Roo (Tigers)</a> on a game named "Civil War Derby" ("Guerra Civil" in Spanish).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saraperos_de_Saltillo" title="Saraperos de Saltillo">Saraperos de Saltillo (Saltillo Sarapemaker's)</a> vs. <a href="/wiki/Vaqueros_Laguna" title="Vaqueros Laguna">Vaqueros Laguna (Torreon Lagoon Cowboys)</a> on a game named "Coahuila's Metropolitan Derby" ("Clásico metropolitano de Coahuila" in Spanish).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pericos_de_Puebla" title="Pericos de Puebla">Pericos de Puebla (Puebla Parakeets)</a> vs. <a href="/wiki/Rojos_del_%C3%81guila_de_Veracruz" title="Rojos del Águila de Veracruz">Rojos del Águila de Veracruz (Veracruz Red Eagles)</a> on a game named "Center rivalry" ("Rivalidad del centro" in Spanish).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
<li>Diablos Rojos del México (Mexico City Red Devils) vs. Péricos de Puebla (Puebla Parakeets) on a game named "Anahuac Derby" ("Clásico de Ánahuac" in Spanish).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<li><a href="/wiki/Naranjeros_de_Hermosillo" title="Naranjeros de Hermosillo">Naranjeros de Hermosillo (Hermosillo Orange)</a> vs. <a href="/wiki/Tomateros_de_Culiac%C3%A1n" title="Tomateros de Culiacán">Tomateros de Culiacán (Culiacan Tomatoes)</a> on a game named "Derby of the Pacific Coast" ("Clásico del pacifico" in Spanish).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></li>

<li id="cite_note-273"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-273">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Preston Lerner (August 2009). "Great Rivalries: Didier Pironi vs. Gilles Villeneuve". <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile_Magazine" title="Automobile Magazine">Automobile Magazine</a></i>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+sports+rivalries&amp;rft.atitle=Great+Rivalries%3A+Didier+Pironi+vs.+Gilles+Villeneuve&amp;rft.au=Preston+Lerner&amp;rft.date=2009-08&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Automobile+Magazine&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span> <span class="error citation-comment" style="display:none;font-size:100%">Missing or empty <code style="color:inherit; border:inherit; padding:inherit;">|url=</code> (<a href="/wiki/Help:CS1_errors#cite_web_url" title="Help:CS1 errors">help</a>)</span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-274"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-274">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Rainey's intense rivalry with fellow American and 1993 world champ Kevin Schwantz was the stuff of legends. Their careers progressed together as did their mutual hatred of each other and whether it was in American national races, the Transatlantic Trophy in England or the GPs, they only cared about beating each other, even if that meant coming last and second last.<cite class="citation web">Stuart Barker (18 May 2009). <a class="external text" href="http://www.visordown.com/features/i-love-the-90s/7035.html" rel="nofollow">"I Love The 90s"</a>. Visor Down<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">12 February</span> 2010</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+sports+rivalries&amp;rft.au=Stuart+Barker&amp;rft.btitle=I+Love+The+90s&amp;rft.date=2009-05-18&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.visordown.com%2Ffeatures%2Fi-love-the-90s%2F7035.html&amp;rft.pub=Visor+Down&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-275"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-275">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"How Formula One today could do with a rivalry as bitter and compelling as this one. Two of the greatest drivers of all time, pitted repeatedly against one another. Stylistically they were different, but essentially it was personal."<cite class="citation news">Matt Tench and Jamie Jackson (3 November 2002). <a class="external text" href="http://observer.guardian.co.uk/osm/story/0,,822392,00.html" rel="nofollow">"The top 10 greatest rivalries in the history of sport"</a>. <i>The Observer</i>. London<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">16 February</span> 2010</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+sports+rivalries&amp;rft.atitle=The+top+10+greatest+rivalries+in+the+history+of+sport&amp;rft.au=Matt+Tench+and+Jamie+Jackson&amp;rft.date=2002-11-03&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fobserver.guardian.co.uk%2Fosm%2Fstory%2F0%2C%2C822392%2C00.html&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Observer&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-276"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-276">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Foyt and Andretti were never friends, but neither were they enemies. Ayrton Senna and Alain Prost, by way of contrast, were oil and water. Or maybe gunpowder and a match is a more apt characterization. Their relationship was contentious enough while they were on separate teams, but paired together at the height of McLaren's F1 supremacy, they formed the ugliest – and most perversely compelling – rivalry in motorsports history.<cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://www.automobilemag.com/features/racing/0909_racings_best_rivalries/ayrton_senna_vs_alain_prost.html" rel="nofollow">"Great Rivalries: Racing's Best Rivalries"</a>. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automobile_Magazine" title="Automobile Magazine">Automobile Magazine</a></i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">13 April</span> 2010</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+sports+rivalries&amp;rft.atitle=Great+Rivalries%3A+Racing%27s+Best+Rivalries&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.automobilemag.com%2Ffeatures%2Fracing%2F0909_racings_best_rivalries%2Fayrton_senna_vs_alain_prost.html&amp;rft.jtitle=Automobile+Magazine&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-277"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-277">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Alone at the top – For 2000, Millen's biggest rival, Nobuhiro Tajima will not be competing in the Unlimited Class. Instead, Tajima will bring a new vehicle to the Pikes Peak Open Class. While the overall title is still up for grabs, the six-year rivalry for the class title has ended.<cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://www.motorsport.com/news/article.asp?ID=46467&amp;FS=HILLCLIMB" rel="nofollow">"Above the tree line – Rod Millen Shoots For 10-Minute Barrier"</a>. motorsport.com. 29 June 2000<span class="reference-accessdate">. <li id="cite_note-279"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-279">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">That tussle of 1994 between Russell and Fogarty was the making of the sport as a spectacle that could attract millions. The Brit vs Yank, hard-knock lad vs spoilt brat head-to-head the media constructed around the 1994 season guaranteed an unprecedented level of exposure for Superbikes.<cite class="citation news">Kevin Sampson (26 May 2001). <a class="external text" href="https://www.theguardian.com/theguardian/2001/may/26/weekend7.weekend" rel="nofollow">"Ordinary hero"</a>. <i>The Guardian</i>. <li id="cite_note-281"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-281">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://zeenews.india.com/sports/motorsports/mika-hakkinen-urges-old-rival-michael-schumacher-to-fight-for-recovery_777536.html" rel="nofollow">"Mika Hakkinen urges old rival Michael Schumacher to fight for recovery"</a>. <i>Zee News</i>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+sports+rivalries&amp;rft.atitle=Mika+Hakkinen+urges+old+rival+Michael+Schumacher+to+fight+for+recovery&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fzeenews.india.com%2Fsports%2Fmotorsports%2Fmika-hakkinen-urges-old-rival-michael-schumacher-to-fight-for-recovery_777536.html&amp;rft.jtitle=Zee+News&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-282"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-282">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The season as team mates for rookie Hamilton and defending 2005 and 2006 world champion Alonso ended in the latters' bitter departure from the <a href="/wiki/McLaren" title="McLaren">McLaren</a> team amid conflicts with the team hierarchy with regards to involvement in <a href="/wiki/2007_Formula_One_espionage_controversy" title="2007 Formula One espionage controversy">Spygate</a> and blocking Hamilton in qualifying at one event. The feud also saw drivers take points off each other to allow <a href="/wiki/Kimi_R%C3%A4ikk%C3%B6nen" title="Kimi Räikkönen">Kimi Räikkönen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari" title="Scuderia Ferrari">Ferrari</a> to come from behind to win by a solitary point over both. The two are yet to contest a world championship finale against each other since.<cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://www.telegraph.co.uk/sport/2321358/Lewis-Hamilton-vents-fury-at-Alonso-tactics.html" rel="nofollow">"Lewis Hamilton vents fury at Alonso tactics"</a>. <li id="cite_note-283"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-283">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://indycarnation.indycar.com/exclusive-news/2011/06/28/dixon-vs-franchitti----the-silent-rivalry" rel="nofollow">"Dixon vs. Franchitti -- the silent rivalry"</a>. <i>indycar.com</i>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+sports+rivalries&amp;rft.atitle=Dixon+vs.+Franchitti+--+the+silent+rivalry&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Findycarnation.indycar.com%2Fexclusive-news%2F2011%2F06%2F28%2Fdixon-vs-franchitti----the-silent-rivalry&amp;rft.jtitle=indycar.com&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-284"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-284">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Vettel won four world titles in a row between 2010 and 2013 at <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Racing" title="Red Bull Racing">Red Bull Racing</a>, with Alonso finishing second on three occasions – two of the titles narrowly won in finales, denying Alonso his third title. Then as Alonso left <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari" title="Scuderia Ferrari">Ferrari</a> in late 2014, Vettel signed for the team as his replacement. The rivalry was fierce, yet respectful with few on-track clashes.<cite class="citation web">Andrew Benson (25 November 2012). <a class="external text" href="http://www.bbc.com/sport/0/formula1/20490565" rel="nofollow">"Vettel and Alonso's rivalry becomes one with real teeth"</a>. <li id="cite_note-287"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-287">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Reigning MotoGP world champion Valentino Rossi says he is looking forward to renewing his rivalry with former foe Sete Gibernau in the 2009 MotoGP world championship.<cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://www.motorcyclenews.com/MCN/sport/sportresults/mcn/2008/November/10-16/nov1308-Rossi-looking-forward-to-new-Gibernau-battle/" rel="nofollow">"Valentino Rossi looking forward to new Sete Gibernau battle"</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motorcycle_News" title="Motorcycle News">Motorcycle News</a>. 13 November 2008<span class="reference-accessdate">. <li id="cite_note-288"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-288">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">""The rivalry with Pearson was strictly trying to beat each other," Petty said. You didn't need to with Pearson.""<cite class="citation web">David Newton (29 August 2008). <a class="external text" href="http://sports.espn.go.com/rpm/nascar/cup/columns/story?columnist=newton_david&amp;id=3559664" rel="nofollow">"Top rivalries marked by crashing cars, flying fists and swinging helmets"</a>. <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. <li id="cite_note-289"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-289">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Surpassing these and others is a rivalry forged not so much out of jealousy or bitterness, as much as it was two giants immersed in a supreme struggle for supremacy, because winning is the name of the game. To this observer, the greatest NASCAR rivalry of all time was the ongoing tussle between the man they called “The King,” and the ever sly “Silver Fox."<cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="http://bump-drafts.com/2009/12/27/they-call-him-the-king-part-iii-the-greatest-rivalry/" rel="nofollow">"They Call Him "The King," Part III- The Greatest Rivalry"</a>. 27 December 2009<span class="reference-accessdate">. <li id="cite_note-290"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-290">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"The feud reached a boiling point during the final three laps of a 1972 race at North Wilkesboro (N.C.) Speedway. Petty was leading on Lap 367 when Allison drove low to make a pass. Petty cut him off, using another car to block."<cite class="citation web">David Newton (29 August 2008). <a class="external text" href="http://sports.espn.go.com/rpm/nascar/cup/columns/story?columnist=newton_david&amp;id=3559664" rel="nofollow">"Top rivalries marked by crashing cars, flying fists and swinging helmets"</a>. <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. <li id="cite_note-291"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-291">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"This rivalry was defined by the last lap of the 1979 Daytona 500. Cale Yarborough was fighting Donnie Allison for the lead when, as Yarborough recalls, he was shoved into the infield grass. <li id="cite_note-292"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-292">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"The hatred Allison and Yarborough shared for Waltrip was no secret in the garage. It just kept us from cooperating on any kind of an effort that would have been good for both of us.""<cite class="citation web">David Newton (29 August 2008). <a class="external text" href="http://sports.espn.go.com/rpm/nascar/cup/columns/story?columnist=newton_david&amp;id=3559664" rel="nofollow">"Top rivalries marked by crashing cars, flying fists and swinging helmets"</a>. <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.
